  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_954cb271-92fd-44d0-bcfc-49ac55648db9'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1141149-hi-michael-i-have-bought-the-theft-of">Hi Michael.
I have bought the theft of swords, but I have set aside The crown tower, so I need a definitive start point, any help?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1141149'><a id="like_count_community_question_1141149" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1141149?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F4345290-the-crown-conspiracy">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1141149-hi-michael-i-have-bought-the-theft-of">3 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1141149-hi-michael-i-have-bought-the-theft-of">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1598503-michael"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442493571i/1598503._UX100_CR0,20,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/1598503-michael">Michael</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Sure thing. Reading order is a question I'm often asked. And it's a bit more complicated now that we have 2 books out in Legends. Let me start by talk<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Sure thing. Reading order is a question I'm often asked. And it's a bit more complicated now that we have 2 books out in Legends. Let me start by talking about Riyria: (and whether Revelations or Chronicles should be first).<br /><br />When I wrote The Riyria Revelations (Theft of Swords | Rise of Empire | Heir of Novron), I penned the entire series before publishing the first book. I had a very particular starting point, and a well determined end, and that was all I expected to write.<br /><br />Well, after the series was released, my wife (and others) were lamenting that they missed the pair (Royce and Hadrian - my two main protagonists). Seeing as how Riyria Revelation ended in what I though was a very satisfying manner, I didn't want to "tack on" and risk ruining something that was, in my mind, pretty special. <br /><br />Then it occurred to me that Riyria had been together for twelve years before the first pages of Theft of Swords, so I decided I could "bring them back" if I went to the other end the timeline. In other words, explore in detail how they met and their early years adventuring together. Hence, the Riyria Chronicles was created. Now, because I'm still protective of the pair, I'd rather have them leave too soon than stay around too long. To that end, I don't know how many Chronicle books there will be. I've plotted out an arc that has a total of 11 books, but my moods operandi is to release a book, take the temperature of the readers, and only if it seems like they want more to release another. So, presently that series is kinda "open ended" and the books are much more "stand alone" while Revelations is a single tale broken down into six self-contained episodes. <br /><br />That's a long way of saying there are several things that come into play when deciding what to read.<br /><br />Do you like completed series? - Start with Theft of Swords<br />Do you like to read chronologically? - start with The Crown Tower<br />Do you like reading in order of publication - start with Theft of Swords<br /><br />There are also some other factors, and those make me suggest Theft of Swords first. Here's why:<br /><br />* It's a better value - each book is two full-length novels in one volume, and since all the books cost the same, you get two books for the price of one.<br /><br />* It's the way I wanted to introduce readers to the characters and the world. I start out simply (holding a lot back so I can expose character backgrounds and world building across the whole narrative). And I ramp up the stakes with each subsequent novel. The idea was to make each book better than the previous, and feedback indicates I hit that goal.<br /><br />* I put little Easter eggs in Chronicles for people who have read Revelations. These aren't anything that would affect the plot, just little winks and nods for "people in the know."<br /><br />Now, all that said, I've heard from plenty of readers who have gone "chronologically" as that is their preference and I've yet to hear anyone regret that choice. The consensus seems to be that both orders work (although obviously a slightly different experience as you'll learn certain aspects at different times). But I will say that it was a high priority of mine to make both possible choices work, and I think the jury is in on that and I'm happy to say I hit the goal I was aiming at.<br /><br />So...my suggestion is to start with Theft of Swords, but if you REALLY REALLY enjoy your books in chronological order, than by all means you'll still get a good experience starting with The Crown Tower. <br /><br />Okay, so that covers where to start if you start with Riyria, but what about when you put Legends in the mix. Should you start with Legends or Riyria? Well, both work. Legends is my latest work and therefore "better written" then Theft of Swords which I wrote 13 year ago. But I do have a presence for "reading order." So I would still start with Theft of Swords.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<a href="/questions/453423-is-this-where-i-start-in-michael">Is this where I start in Michael Sullivan&#39;s books? I purchased Theft of Swords and was going to start reading, but there was an author&#39;s note recommending not starting with Theft of Swords. 
This is on my summer reading list, and have read great reviews... would love to get started!</a>
</div>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1598503-michael"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442493571i/1598503._UX100_CR0,20,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You may be confused between "The Crown Tower" and "The Crown Conspiracy." <br/><br/>* The Crown Conspiracy is book #1 of the Riyria Revelations and it can be fo<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You may be confused between "The Crown Tower" and "The Crown Conspiracy." <br /><br />* The Crown Conspiracy is book #1 of the Riyria Revelations and it can be found as the first novel in the Theft of Swords Omnibus (which also includes Avempartha)<br /><br />* The Crown Tower is book #1 of the Riyria Chronicles, and yes in that book I mentioned you should start with Theft of Swords rather than The Crown Tower.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_45399626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45399626" />
    <a title="Sandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/811687-sandi"><img alt="Sandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404709147p2/811687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45399626?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandi" href="/user/show/811687-sandi">Sandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45399626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4758492885034665644">I have a problem with fantasy. I do like the genre, but I can't stand multi-volume epics with 900+ pages per volume. I don't like spending 25 pages in a cave or 150 pages fighting a battle. I don't need a six-page description of a tavern. I don't like struggling to figure out how a name is pronounced. Since the fantasy genre seems to be dominated by what I don't like, I tend to approach it with extreme caution. <br/><br/>In my opinion, fantasy authors and publishers could take some lessons from Michael Su</span>
  <span id="freeText4758492885034665644" style="display:none">I have a problem with fantasy. I do like the genre, but I can't stand multi-volume epics with 900+ pages per volume. I don't like spending 25 pages in a cave or 150 pages fighting a battle. I don't need a six-page description of a tavern. I don't like struggling to figure out how a name is pronounced. Since the fantasy genre seems to be dominated by what I don't like, I tend to approach it with extreme caution. <br /><br />In my opinion, fantasy authors and publishers could take some lessons from Michael Sullivan's "The Crown Conspiracy." If we could give half stars, I'd give this 4-1/2. Sullivan does a fabulous job of creating a believable world and credible characters without using a ton of exposition. In one sentence, he manages to convey as much as many writers do in 50 pages. The story is fast-paced, unpredictable, and entertaining. It's clear that Sullivan has done his research. His battle scenes are realistically gruesome. I liked how the characters interconnected. I loved the subtly humorous touches.<br /><br />To me, the best part is when the main characters go to see the wizard in the secret prison. The wizard has been locked up for 900 years and the way he communicates with the heroes is realistic and funny. How often do you ever think about the language barrier 900 years can cause?<br /><br />I highly recommend "The Crown Conspiracy" for anyone who likes fantasy but doesn't want to get bogged down in an endless series. It is a done-in-one story that leaves plenty of opportunity for both author and reader to revisit that world at any time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4758492885034665644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2084613945?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=advanture">advanture</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2084613945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8225054538397101439"><b>*** 4.25 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with my friends at BB&B!</b><br/><br/>You know how some authors feel like they are working on your wave-length​? Well, I think MJS is one of those for me. I love his storytelling style, natural and easy, never jumping into melodramatic nor falling to pedestrian. It is always just the way my senses need it to be. And this is exactly how I like my Fantasy Adventures to be told - with a perfect feel for timing, pacing and a sense of humor. Add an exceptional talent for banter and underst</span>
  <span id="freeText8225054538397101439" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.25 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with my friends at BB&amp;B!</b><br /><br />You know how some authors feel like they are working on your wave-length​? Well, I think MJS is one of those for me. I love his storytelling style, natural and easy, never jumping into melodramatic nor falling to pedestrian. It is always just the way my senses need it to be. And this is exactly how I like my Fantasy Adventures to be told - with a perfect feel for timing, pacing and a sense of humor. Add an exceptional talent for banter and understated emotional relationships, and you have one of my favorite new authors, whose work has become a must read for me. <br /><br />This is a re-read for me and it was just as fun the second time around. I love the thieving duo of Royce and Hadrian, aka Riyria, who make for one of the best bromance couples in recent years. They complete each other both in character and physical abilities, as well as areas of expertise when it comes to the art of stealing. They also have a talent of getting in trouble spectacularly! The two of them together are bigger than life, enigmatic and completely lovable. However, in this book, my heart was stolen by the diminutive autistic monk Myron ❤! There is something so tender and innocent, so good and gentle in that weird guy, that I couldn't get enough of him on page! I need more and more, and am grateful to Michael for giving us his time at the end of the book!!!<br /><br />The story is not complicated, but perfectly paced and just enough to get us hooked on the series. The thieves are hired to steal something from the Castle and get framed for murder. In order to save their lives, they agree to help by abducting the Prince and take him to meet an imprisoned Wizard. Everything else happens around this basic arc. It is interesting, well crafted and a lot of fun. I recommend it to everyone 😀😀😀!!!<br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and many more wonderful books to come!!!</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_100276024" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100276024" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100276024?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of shorter fantasy novels</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=amiable-rogues">amiable-rogues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=warrior">warrior</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2013-200s-club-challenge">2013-200s-club-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=antihero">antihero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=dynamic-duo">dynamic-duo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=plan-to-read-soon">plan-to-read-soon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=reluctant-or-unlikely-hero">reluctant-or-unlikely-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100276024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7528941235676376294">The Crown Conspiracy is perfect for readers who enjoy epic fantasy, but in a smaller package. When you have the time and energy for a 500 or more page epic, why not? But if you want a good historical fantasy tale that is shorter but doesn't lack what you enjoy in the genre, then it's great to find one. This is a good choice if you have encountered that dilemma. When I developed a renewed taste for fantasy as an adult reader, I looked at different fantasy novels that many established fans of the </span>
  <span id="freeText7528941235676376294" style="display:none">The Crown Conspiracy is perfect for readers who enjoy epic fantasy, but in a smaller package. When you have the time and energy for a 500 or more page epic, why not? But if you want a good historical fantasy tale that is shorter but doesn't lack what you enjoy in the genre, then it's great to find one. This is a good choice if you have encountered that dilemma. When I developed a renewed taste for fantasy as an adult reader, I looked at different fantasy novels that many established fans of the genre recommended, and this one continually came up. I've had this on my to read pile for years, and fortunately, my library had a copy. I had a ball reading it.<br /><br /><b> Characters</b>:<br /><br />A good writer can use an economy of words and bring a character to life. Most of my favorite authors are ones who excel at this. I would say Sullivan acquitted himself very well in this area. The portrayal of characters in this novel gave me what I need but also left some mystery. Some characters more than others. He reveals most of their personalities through what they do and say, instead of in long descriptions of them or telling their histories. That's okay with me. I like a story that keeps moving. <br /><br /> As far as characters that stood out the most: <br /><br /> I definitely want to see more of Esrahraddon. But then wizards have that effect on you. The more mysterious the better. Besides Hadrian and Royce, the lead characters, I have to say my favorite was Myron. His sense of wonder about the world (which makes sense considering he was in a monastery for over 30 years and most of his life at the age of 36). He has some of the funniest lines in the book. He's utterly captivated by horses, for instance. He's never seen one before, and he thinks they are brilliant. The same goes for women. You can't help but laugh at him, but it's in a gentle way, because he's really a sweet guy.<br /><br /> Other characters grow on you, such as Prince Alric. He's pretty much a pompous jerk initially. But he comes into his own. You realize that he's not different from Myron. Merely a person shaped by his experiences. He comes to realize that being King is not just luxury and privilege, but also a lot of responsibility and discomfort and self-sacrifice. He learns that the hard way. He also learns who he can trust, and that is not always who he might initially think.<br /><br />Hadrian and Royce are two of those amiable rogues that make fantasy so fun. They are thieves and proud. But they have honor, in their own way. I like how they end up saving a kingdom, the unlikely heroes of this piece. Although they might be criminals, they are never the bad guys in this book. I liked that distinction. Sometimes you can be on the wrong side of the law and not be a bad person (I am not advocating breaking the law, mind you). Sometimes that law isn’t necessarily fair across the board or makes it hard for you to do what’s right. Or maybe you’re just a criminal who is otherwise a decent person. I don’t see why it can’t happen, at least in theory. <br /><br />I liked that the characters’ motives aren’t necessarily crystal clear initially. You have to read to see the story develop (sounds like a no-brainer) and what choices the characters make that will define them ultimately, or at least elucidate who they are. There were some nice twists and turns along the way that I wasn't expecting. While some of the secondary characters are less developed, that’s only to be expected, unless you want a 1000 page book, and I definitely don’t.<br /><br /><b>The World of this Novel and Magic</b>:<br /><br />What could have been complex world-building instead is simply explained, which is a relief. I like books that have good world-building, but I don’t like things so complicated that I can’t figure out what’s going on or I am drawn out of the story and get bored. The political themes are a constant undercurrent of the story as there is a struggle between the imperialists, nationalists, and royalists, and the main characters get caught up in this struggle on a personal level. The religious foundations and spiritual beliefs of these countries also play a role in the storyline, since the governments are more or less based on the founding/creating gods worshiped. When Myron explained all this to Royce and Hadrian, I admit I was captivated. It made sense, and at the same time, it was rather sophisticated how the ancient past related to the present of the world at the time of this book. Albeit subtle in rendering, magic is part and parcel of this world, used as another instrument to wield for everyday uses. I especially loved Esrahaddon's prison. It was unnerving and yet fascinating that magic allowed such an invention. And the fact that they would go to so much trouble just to keep one person locked up made me long for more information about this unique individual. I wish that Astria had been able to demonstrate more magical ability. She only got to do a couple of simple magical things, and with her role being so important to the story, it would have been nice to see more of her. Perhaps Sullivan didn’t want magic to be a fix all in this book. With that as a presumption, I can understand why he kept magic low key in the story overall.<br /><br />Overall, I was quite satisfied with this story. I think it was a very good fantasy adventure tale. While I have read some epic fantasy stories that have more wow factor, I think this is one that sneaks in on you and delivers in a way that can’t be questioned. It harkens back to the older adventure tales, such as Fafhrd and The Gray Mouser by Fitz Leiber or even Elric of Melnibone’ by Michael Moorcock. Shorter stories that are great reads in their own way even if they don’t seem as majestic as Tolkien. From reading this work, I would say that Sullivan definitely has a love of this genre, and he created a story that treats it with respect. <br /><br />I definitely want to follow this series, and it’s gratifying that these books were written in such a way that they are self-contained despite being related to each other. I would recommend The Crown Conspiracy to fantasy readers, and those who want to give the genre a try.<br /><br />Overall rating: <b>4.5/5.0 stars</b>.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="7528941235676376294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2818406029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2818406029" />
    <a title="Allison Hurd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd"><img alt="Allison Hurd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530670583p2/14495279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2818406029?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison Hurd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison Hurd" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd">Allison Hurd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=sff-bookshelf">sff-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=sff-2019-challenge">sff-2019-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=man-author">man-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2818406029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15808786009852079122">I originally started reading <i>Theft of Swords</i> but quickly changed my goal to a more manageable one. This review is not going to be popular. It might even cause some hurt, for which I am sorry. Usually I give my overall impression first, but this time I want to say that this isn't meant to be a personal attack on anyone. From my limited interaction with Michael, he seems a pleasant, conscientious person. And I have many friends who found honest enjoyment in this book. I am not suggesting anything </span>
  <span id="freeText15808786009852079122" style="display:none">I originally started reading <i>Theft of Swords</i> but quickly changed my goal to a more manageable one. This review is not going to be popular. It might even cause some hurt, for which I am sorry. Usually I give my overall impression first, but this time I want to say that this isn't meant to be a personal attack on anyone. From my limited interaction with Michael, he seems a pleasant, conscientious person. And I have many friends who found honest enjoyment in this book. I am not suggesting anything about the character of anyone who enjoyed this--God knows I have problematic things that I just adore, pip, core, bigotry and all. If you loved this and don't want to hear someone rage about the state of the world and what this book demonstrates regarding it, I don't blame you. Come back later, I have 2 books I'm reading next that I think will get much more level-headed responses! <br /><br />If you want a rant, though, grab some popcorn.<br /><br />Now that that's out of the way, I hated this. I found reasons not to read it, like paying bills, skimmed when I could and winced when I couldn't. This is an epic example of how characters like our anti-heroes can be "good" but also perpetuate the absolutely disgusting mindsets about people which characterizes "the nice guy." You know the one, the guy who would never hit a woman, opens doors with a slight bow to "m'lady" and then calls her a bitch when she doesn't blush and smile gratefully and wonders why that woman would go for someone else when he's over here, holding doors and bowing and all he wants is a little bit of simpering or sex. Also, one of his best friends is a person of color who allows him to use slurs, so it's okay if he says it. For me, this book was those interactions over and over and over.<br /><br /><b>CONTENT WARNING</b>: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ torture, misogyny, fantasy racism, body horror, rape jokes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Things I'd stop skimming to read:</u><br /><br />-<b>Hadrian and Royce</b>. They were your typical plucky duo, there was sufficient witty banter to be entertaining.<br /><br />-<b>Myron</b>. Up until he met a girl, he was very cute, albeit unbelievable in just about all regards.<br /><br />-<b>Any woman talking</b>. I kept hoping they'd do something that put someone in their place. No such luck, but I got my hopes up a few times.<br /><br /><u>Okay, buckle up, this is where I trash things:</u><br /><br />-<b>This is what casual sexism looks like</b>. There are no women who are respected and have both agency and purpose in this story. I thought I'd met one, and then got angry this wasn't her story as it sounded way more interesting. But then, as usual, any woman with an air of competence must be rescued and/or doted upon. But wait! This time there's even a rape joke! Hur hur, bet the <i>five male gods</i> and their raped daughter/sister/wife who is the only divine woman in their mythology have awkward family dinners! Seriously, every woman mentioned was literally one of the archetypes of whore, mother, virgin, and witch, and all of them were either aghast at each other or suddenly forgot how to be humans the second a man looked at them. And let's not forget to reeeeally commit to the "love what you loathe" mentality and take wild potshots at sex workers, too. This is the kind of thing I thought had died by the time Polgara took the stage, but apparently we're in that phase of readership where women being a compilation if hips, lips, and quips for the benefit of their manly companions is now "classic" or "nostalgic" or "cute." I am probably about as upset with the response as I am with the set up, to be quite frank. It shows me how far we have yet to go, and, my friends, <i>we have so far to go.</i><br /><br />-<b>Take a little more bigotry, too</b>. This suffers from the classic fantasy genocide. Where are the brown people? The main characters are called humans, they're diurnal and their planet orbits a single star, so it stands to reason they'd have the same pigmentation variation as any other humans. As there is not, I assume something happened to all of them, and if we're being "historically accurate" as I'm guessing this was intended to be, the thing that happened likely wasn't good. Boo. Hiss. Furthermore, where are anyone who isn't a virile male intent on proving how durn-tootin' big his dick is? There's subtle queer antagonism (or misogyny, depending on how you want to view it, I support the argument that it's both) in the forms of mocking men who are not in competition with other men and even the quintessential "yew 'it loik a girl!" type comments. Want more? How about evil dwarves who are just obviously maniacal because...well because! And elves who were enslaved. And like, our good guys must be good because they give one of the abused half elves a horse. I mean, they also casually discuss the difference between slavery and indentured servitude while that half elf is trying to buy food in the face of imminent danger to his safety, but c'mon, I watched the first third of American Psycho and that Patrick fella really stood up for marginalized people at dinner, so I'm sure he was a great human who followed through on his convictions whenever he had a spare horse to give.<br /><br />Well that was longer than I intended, but this is my review space and those are my thoughts. I don't find this appealing, I find it hard to accept in this digital age when we can see in real time the plight of actual people who are different from us, and have so many tools we can use to help. In a fantasy setting, when there are no real consequences for being a Big Damn Hero, having "help the wretched" not be part of the power fantasy is a huge turn off for me. If you're gonna have slavery in your book, let's be real about that, too, and then get bigger than life about the payback, too.<br /><br />-<b>As purple as any YA</b>. It takes a master for me to get swept away in seas of adjectives. I could and did skim most of the scenery here as easily as I did girls talking about their heaps of precious gowns and whatever manly smell we like in books these days--leather and soap I think? Anyways, it felt like stock imagery for the most part and aside from knowing who was present and roughly where they were, the rest felt like it could have been trimmed down or made a lot more interesting. I have thoughts on why this book didn't get slammed like those books do, but I'm in a pretty vehemently Ani DiFranco headspace right now so I'll keep that to myself until I've returned this book to the library and have nothing in my line of sight that reminds me of my rage.<br /><br />-<b>The wizard</b>. Holy crap this was annoying. He talked like Yoda if Yoda was also a drunk failure of a Shakespearean wannabe. There are rules to thee and thou and sentence structure from older English. They weren't followed, let alone any explanation given for its use now. Dude's been talking to an erudite woman competent enough to learn what he can teach for over a year, I think he's seen how things go.<br /><br />-<b>Caricatures, not characters</b>. You'll know whodunnit almost instantly, and you'll know more or less how they'll undo it about as quick. Make sure you look out for your favorite trope, be it Ignorant Villager, Sheltered Monk, Devious Wizard, Whore With A Heart of Gold, Man with a Past etc. etc. They're all there, wave as you drive by. <br /><br />-<b>The MCs weren't even that cool!!!</b> Tragedy of tragedy, our extra competent heroes aren't actually super competent. They continuously need people to point out things to them, get caught in ridiculous traps, take actions that even basic education via other books in the genre would point out as bad ideas, and miraculously land on their feet. We're supposed to be in awe of their wherewithal, but I spent most of the time going "so their real power is an author who loves them." And that last line. Oy. I can see them both scrawling that and then turning to the camera, backs together, arms crossed, flat-brimmed ball caps and plastic sunglasses tilted just so.<br /><br />I can't finish <i>Theft of Swords.</i> I did my best to finish one book to give it a fair shake and I'm so mad I don't think I should talk to anyone for awhile. This is everything that sets my teeth on edge in fantasy and I guess in that, well done. I'm quite ready to snarl if anyone would like a good glance at a girl gone mad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15808786009852079122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=sword-and-sorcery">sword-and-sorcery</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer50424676&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50424676" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17563304424799354579">An enjoyable enough book, but nothing that wowed me. It was generally well-paced, but it also wasn't a book that I couldn't put down... <br/><br/>I think one of my complaints was that there wasn't really a lot of character development - it's very much a plot-based book. Which is fine, for what it is - I just, personally, tend to prefer more depth in characters. I felt it was kind of standard "reluctant thief, jovial merc, brat prince thrown into power... Go!"<br/><br/>There were also a few little technical points w</span>
  <span id="freeText17563304424799354579" style="display:none">An enjoyable enough book, but nothing that wowed me. It was generally well-paced, but it also wasn't a book that I couldn't put down... <br /><br />I think one of my complaints was that there wasn't really a lot of character development - it's very much a plot-based book. Which is fine, for what it is - I just, personally, tend to prefer more depth in characters. I felt it was kind of standard "reluctant thief, jovial merc, brat prince thrown into power... Go!"<br /><br />There were also a few little technical points which annoyed me. <br /><br /><br />*Might contain slight spoilers*<br /><br />When the explained how they got the letters, I felt this could've been better if it was more show and less tell. There was that problem in a few places.<br /><br />The language difference of Esrahaddon, while an understandable and interesting part of the world-building, was a bit awkward. Language would change more in 900 years that a few (sometimes awkwardly placed) thees and thous... and a few altered words. I mean, look at the difference between Chaucer and modern English... and that's, what, a little over 600 years?<br /><br />And, as someone else mentioned, would a monk whose read a hundred... a thousand books... who remembers everything he reads... really have never come across anything which mentions that horses can be brown, but not blue or green?<br /><br />I thought the intrigue of who the real traitor was could've been dragged out a bit more... perhaps a less obvious red herring, some more options for who it could've been... Maybe interspersed more throughout the whole story, instead of two or three chapters in succession... <br /><br />Oh, and one last thing... the whole thing at the end when they attacked the castle, and then Alric reveals himself. I kept thinking how stupid that whole thing was. I mean, they mention that he had his banner or something. How could the people on the gates not know it was him? Or, heck, why wouldn't he try and reveal his identity before releasing arrows on the city? Some sort of parlay, or something? Heck, if he had come in more quietly and revealed himself at the trial, he could've avoided the whole thing.<br /><br />I just felt that whole part was kind of silly... It didn't make a whole lot of logical sense to me... <br /><br />*End spoilers*<br /><br /><br />Anyway, some of them are minor quibbles... some things distracted me while I was reading, 'cause I kept focusing on how awkward or odd something was, instead of being truly invested in the story...<br /><br />That and I didn't particulary care that much for any of the characters... and I never really felt they were ever in any real kind of danger... <br /><br /><br />But, um, yes... Still generally entertaining. I didn't dislike it... I just wasn't all that impressed with it, either... I will probably read the next in the series, though, in the hopes that the characters will be fleshed out more as the series continues... </span>
  <a data-text-id="17563304424799354579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14476724254655710055">I'm all about grim dark , complex, dense epic fantasy, I really didn't think i'd enjoy this as much as i did. <br/>The world building was well done, Elan is a beautiful world with rich history and myths. To me the best aspect of this novel was how well defined the characters were. Royce, Hadrian, Alric, Myron...even the antagonists, they all had unique personalities. <br/>As for the story itself, its been a while I've felt this compelled by a book. I couldn't put it down once I started. Given the recent s</span>
  <span id="freeText14476724254655710055" style="display:none">I'm all about grim dark , complex, dense epic fantasy, I really didn't think i'd enjoy this as much as i did. <br />The world building was well done, Elan is a beautiful world with rich history and myths. To me the best aspect of this novel was how well defined the characters were. Royce, Hadrian, Alric, Myron...even the antagonists, they all had unique personalities. <br />As for the story itself, its been a while I've felt this compelled by a book. I couldn't put it down once I started. Given the recent string of books I've read, it was like a welcomed breath of fresh air and it deserves 5 stars for overall enjoyment.<br /></span>

<div id="review_227036964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227036964" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227036964?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227036964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10468304019113800366">Okay, in the spirit of complete disclosure I actually read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_2_' title='Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Theft of Swords</a> which includes this book and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342483.Avempartha__The_Riyria_Revelations___2_' title='Avempartha (The Riyria Revelations, #2) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Avempartha</a>. Last night however I finished The Crown Conspiracy and have to say I'm exceedingly pleased.<br/><br/>Of late I've read a string of mediocre books. They weren't "bad", I didn't hate them but neither could I get into them. Often I'd get to the point I just didn't care. That's not the case here and if the quality holds up I may become a fan of Mr. Sullivan.<br/><br/>The characters here are not only "well</span>
  <span id="freeText10468304019113800366" style="display:none">Okay, in the spirit of complete disclosure I actually read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_2_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Theft of Swords</a> which includes this book and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342483.Avempartha__The_Riyria_Revelations___2_" title="Avempartha (The Riyria Revelations, #2) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Avempartha</a>. Last night however I finished The Crown Conspiracy and have to say I'm exceedingly pleased.<br /><br />Of late I've read a string of mediocre books. They weren't "bad", I didn't hate them but neither could I get into them. Often I'd get to the point I just didn't care. That's not the case here and if the quality holds up I may become a fan of Mr. Sullivan.<br /><br />The characters here are not only "well drawn" and complete (and we're still filling out our "heroes") but they work well. They stay true to themselves so you begin to get to know them. The secondary or support characters are also well written. They're complete but getting to know them doesn't take pages and pages of back story it shows up as we get the plot.<br /><br />Yes, there's a plot, a good concise well laid out plot that balances with the characterization and doesn't compete with it. The book is I think while light and definitely escapism very well written and highly enjoyable.<br /><br />Believe me I've been in a funk lately and for this book to draw me in and get me involved now says it's interesting and well done. <br /><br />Here we meet our two protagonists Royce and Hadrian a couple of wise cracking....entrepreneurs. Yes that's what they are, "self employed independent contractors" who work for themselves and are generally willing to sign for whoever pays them well enough.<br /><br />Of course some people would call them thieves..scoundrels, on occasion even...assassins. These two are well known by what is apparently their their "company or business name" Riyria. And as noted they work for who pays the best. Did they steal something from you that you were sure was impossible to reach and you thought was surely safe? That's okay. For a big enough paycheck they'll steal it back for you from their previous employer...<br /><br />So, how do these two end up being....the good guys? What string of unplanned "good deeds" could ever land them in the situation of risking their lives to do the right thing? (For proper pay of course).<br /><br />I think you'll like this one. It looks like the opening salvo in what I hope is a great epic fantasy and I can't wait to get back into the story.<br /><br />This one I do highly recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10468304019113800366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376930384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3451297673592220451"><i>The Crown Conspiracy</i> was an interesting book. It was a great start to the series and I already have fallen in love with some characters, like Royce and Hadrian. They are, of course, experienced thieves. They steal from the rich.. and basically give it to other rich people? So don't think of them like good ole' Robin Hood.. because they aren't. However, I still loved the shit out of those two. <br/><br/>Now I can't say who I love more out of this awesome duo but I did enjoy getting to know them. They are c</span>
  <span id="freeText3451297673592220451" style="display:none"><i>The Crown Conspiracy</i> was an interesting book. It was a great start to the series and I already have fallen in love with some characters, like Royce and Hadrian. They are, of course, experienced thieves. They steal from the rich.. and basically give it to other rich people? So don't think of them like good ole' Robin Hood.. because they aren't. However, I still loved the shit out of those two. <br /><br />Now I can't say who I love more out of this awesome duo but I did enjoy getting to know them. They are complete opposites of each other but that's why they work so well. Hadrian is completely lovable yet kind of scary - no, not personality wise but the amount of swords he carries on a daily basis would scare the heck out of me. I wouldn't be able to handle one sword.. let alone three.<br /><br />Then there's Royce who is rough around the edges. He's tough on the outside but once you get to know him.. well, he's basically a teddy bear. I did love his dry sense of humor and when him and Hadrian would banter I couldn't stop smiling or laughing. They were enjoyable to read about and their friendship was pure gold in my eyes.<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed their story and journey throughout the book. I feel like it was missing something extra but I did still fall in love with everything. <br /><br />This book also made me think of others books that combined together and made this baby. It's like the lord of the rings and game of thrones got together and made the crown conspiracy. Just go with me on this people! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3451297673592220451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_51251311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51251311" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51251311?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51251311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8033437396533418699">16Mar2012: the 6th book finally came out in Jan of this year, so I'm re-reading the series in order. I hadn't realized it had been 3 years since I first started reading this series. I didn't read it in order nor did I read the final copy, except this book. I started out by ARC reading book 2, then read this book, then ARC read the rest of the series except book 6. IOW, I get to read this just for fun this time & enjoyed it very much.<br/><br/>-------<br/><br/>4April2009: It's a fun, quick fantasy read. The setting </span>
  <span id="freeText8033437396533418699" style="display:none">16Mar2012: the 6th book finally came out in Jan of this year, so I'm re-reading the series in order. I hadn't realized it had been 3 years since I first started reading this series. I didn't read it in order nor did I read the final copy, except this book. I started out by ARC reading book 2, then read this book, then ARC read the rest of the series except book 6. IOW, I get to read this just for fun this time &amp; enjoyed it very much.<br /><br />-------<br /><br />4April2009: It's a fun, quick fantasy read. The setting is pretty much medieval with magic, dwarfs &amp; elves. A strong church conflicts with nobility in a way that leads me to believe we'll see more of this as the series progresses &amp; was quite logical &amp; realistic. Basically, this book is setting up the rest, almost a prologue. There is plenty of action though, which is often lacking in a prologue. <br /><br />The characters are very likable or hateable, with out much in between, although we do see the development of one from a spoiled brat into a fairly worthy person. The heroes are likable rouges cloaked in some mystery. They're a little too good to be doing what they do, but there is a logical reason for it, we're shown. There is a fair amount of mystery surrounding another character that I'm sure will become a big player later on. The few female characters show some complexity &amp; depth. Their place in society is definitely that of second rate citizens, typical of the setting, yet they are strong enough to fight against it. Each character has their strengths &amp; weaknesses. They demonstrate them, we're not just told about them.<br /><br />I read the second novel first &amp; then this one. It didn't ruin the story for me, but knowing what I do now, I'd like to go back &amp; read the second book again. I know have knowledge about the world that was hinted at &amp; referred to. I hate it when an author spends too much time recapping the previous story. That wasn't done, which I appreciate.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8033437396533418699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338649902?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ChopinFC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ChopinFC" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc">ChopinFC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338649902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2514077354177562063"><br/><b><br/>4 1/2 stars<br/><br/>Michael Sullivan does it again! The first installment of the 'Riyria Revelations', is as much as fun as one can get in the 'fantasy genre'! </b><br/><br/>The book is the first ever written book in the 'Riyria series', and Sullivan does a brilliant job in creating a fast read, with meaningful characters and an engaging enough plot that will leave the reader coming back for more!<br/><br/>In 'The Crown Conspiracy ', we see the creation of one of the most devilishly fun pair of thieves, in 'Hadrian Blackwater' </span>
  <span id="freeText2514077354177562063" style="display:none"><br /><b><br />4 1/2 stars<br /><br />Michael Sullivan does it again! The first installment of the 'Riyria Revelations', is as much as fun as one can get in the 'fantasy genre'! </b><br /><br />The book is the first ever written book in the 'Riyria series', and Sullivan does a brilliant job in creating a fast read, with meaningful characters and an engaging enough plot that will leave the reader coming back for more!<br /><br />In 'The Crown Conspiracy ', we see the creation of one of the most devilishly fun pair of thieves, in 'Hadrian Blackwater' and 'Royce Melbourne'! The book is established in a typical fantasy world, where medieval castles, kings, dukes and earls represent nobility and horses and carriages are your favorite means of transportation. Royce a skilled thief, and his mercenary partner, Hadrian are two enterprising rogues who end up running for their lives when they're framed for the murder of the king.<br /><br /><br />Ultimately what makes 'The Crown Tower' a real 'gem' is how the book blends two characters that are so polar opporsites, yet they complement each other beautifully! Sullivan really want to prove the point that opposites do indeed attract! <br /><br />Hadrian is righteous in every way. He's an ex soldier with great brute power and amazing sword fighting skills. Despite his size and dexterity, he's gentle in nature and tend to believe in people despite their shortcomings. He's a true 'gentle giant'. Royce on the other hand is a dirty scoundrel of an assassin, with a much smaller physique, yet he is extremely agile and cunning. Royce always has a dark hood on, bringing an eerie sense of mystique and danger. Together, both characters are almost like 'oil' and 'water', and despite their fundamental differences, we see them form an organic yet quite counter intuitive union that will propel them into both 'Chronicle' and 'Revelation' series!<br /><br /><b>For a fun, well written fantasy series, with an incredibly well connected linear plot and engaging characters, 'The Riyria Revelation' series is a must read! The first book 'The Crown Conspiracy' will not disappoint!<br /><br />4 1/2 Stars<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></b></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241798527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9089236539659100988">A while ago I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12746970.The_Viscount_and_the_Witch__Riyria_Chronicles___1_5_' title='The Viscount and the Witch (Riyria Chronicles, #1.5) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Viscount and the Witch</a> which was really great. I really liked Royce and Hadrian, they made me laugh many times throughout that short story. Writing a good short story is quite a feat that only few authors have. <br/><br/>The Crown Conspiracy was even better than I had expected. Royce and Hadrian are really great characters, they make a very interesting (and hilarious) team. While Hadrian is a righteous ex-soldier, Royce is a cynical thief with a devious mind, and these two guys make</span>
  <span id="freeText9089236539659100988" style="display:none">A while ago I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12746970.The_Viscount_and_the_Witch__Riyria_Chronicles___1_5_" title="The Viscount and the Witch (Riyria Chronicles, #1.5) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Viscount and the Witch</a> which was really great. I really liked Royce and Hadrian, they made me laugh many times throughout that short story. Writing a good short story is quite a feat that only few authors have. <br /><br />The Crown Conspiracy was even better than I had expected. Royce and Hadrian are really great characters, they make a very interesting (and hilarious) team. While Hadrian is a righteous ex-soldier, Royce is a cynical thief with a devious mind, and these two guys make a great team, and Ocean 11 instantly pops to my mind when I think about this team. Both are extremely capable, each in his own way. The supporting characters are quite good, and they evolve though the book, which was nice because in some books the supporting characters are somewhat weak.<br /><br />As for the plot - it gets better as you keep reading. Until 70% mark it was quite good, though it gets better while there's lots of intrigue and schemes are unravel which makes things more interesting. It also seems like the series can expand and become really epic. Plus, the pace is great, it's a very action-oriented book.<br />Now I'm proceeding with Theft of Swords.<br /><br />All in all, it's a really fun read, and although there're some fantasy tropes they don't manifest in a traditional way.<br /><br />4.5/5</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer465562652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10490703525041811070">Is this a tribute to Fafhrd and the Gray Mouser? If not, it should be.<br/><br/>This book has received a fair share of glowing reviews, with reviewers praising, among other things, its lack of unnecessary exposition. And it <i>is</i> an enjoyable book, for the most part. However, <b>some</b> attention to detail would not have been amiss.<br/><br/>Is this a Young Adult novel? I’m not sure. Everything is just skimmed over. We hardly have any idea what anybody looks like or how things work. This is a shame, really, since there are </span>
  <span id="freeText10490703525041811070" style="display:none">Is this a tribute to Fafhrd and the Gray Mouser? If not, it should be.<br /><br />This book has received a fair share of glowing reviews, with reviewers praising, among other things, its lack of unnecessary exposition. And it <i>is</i> an enjoyable book, for the most part. However, <b>some</b> attention to detail would not have been amiss.<br /><br />Is this a Young Adult novel? I’m not sure. Everything is just skimmed over. We hardly have any idea what anybody looks like or how things work. This is a shame, really, since there are some intriguing concepts here. I was especially curious about the nature of Esrahaddon’s abilities.<br /> <br />It’s a quick read, which redeems it. The story is fun and interesting and I did enjoy it, although I <i>did</i> feel that the battle sequence at the castle could have been handled better.<br /><br />Despite what everyone is going on about, I’m not convinced that this breaks any new ground, and there is almost zero character development worth mentioning, but I am still intrigued enough to read the next book in the series, which does say <i>something</i>. <br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3270072443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15052769666698037955">I wanted to read this series and give Michael Sullivan a second chance not having liked the first two books of the legends of the first empire. <br/> <br/>The Crown Conspiracy was fun, however it lacked depth. The characters weren’t developed properly, we barely know anything about their character beyond the obvious. Although Arista’s chapters were few, I was able to learn more about her as a person more than the rest (and I don’t mean it in a good way, like the rest are more mysterious, but they are kind</span>
  <span id="freeText15052769666698037955" style="display:none">I wanted to read this series and give Michael Sullivan a second chance not having liked the first two books of the legends of the first empire. <br /> <br />The Crown Conspiracy was fun, however it lacked depth. The characters weren’t developed properly, we barely know anything about their character beyond the obvious. Although Arista’s chapters were few, I was able to learn more about her as a person more than the rest (and I don’t mean it in a good way, like the rest are more mysterious, but they are kinda lacking? The monk wasn’t bad and even Alric, mostly Royce and Hadrian <i>who are supposed to be the main characters</i>). I didn’t hate them for sure just hoped to learn more about their motives or their personality at least.<br /><br />Just like legends of the first empire we have new names from our world, it makes less sense now having these names 1000 years ago too. At least he could’ve written them differently, like vyctor instead of Victor.. <br /><br />I’ll definitely be continuing this series, I hope it gets better. The premise is already more interesting than that of Legends of the First Empire. The books are short too and not heavy. The writing style is engaging and even the humor isn’t bad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15052769666698037955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_449483065" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/449483065" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5586102-the-crown-conspiracy">review of another edition</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer449483065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3949518188268011848"><i>“It’s those thieves, those damned thieves,” the Earl of Chadwick called out as he ran after Braga. “They’re demons! Magicians! Evil mages! They are like smoke, appearing and disappearing at will.”</i><br/><br/><br/>Hadrian and Royce are Riyria - professional thieves extraordinaire. They steal from the rich, and give to...the other rich...or whoever's rich enough to pay for the job - usually nobles who want special items from other nobles. And they say thieves have no honour!<br/><br/>This is sword and sorcery - rogues and w</span>
  <span id="freeText3949518188268011848" style="display:none"><i>“It’s those thieves, those damned thieves,” the Earl of Chadwick called out as he ran after Braga. “They’re demons! Magicians! Evil mages! They are like smoke, appearing and disappearing at will.”</i><br><br><br>Hadrian and Royce are Riyria - professional thieves extraordinaire. They steal from the rich, and give to...the other rich...or whoever's rich enough to pay for the job - usually nobles who want special items from other nobles. And they say thieves have no honour!<br><br>This is sword and sorcery - rogues and wizards - dwarves and elves...<br><br>Well...there was <i>A</i> dwarf<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385814894i/7235700.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No not Tyrion. Get lost Lannister.<br><br>And there was <i>one</i> elf<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385815123i/7235726.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thank you Legolas - now take your money and rack off pretty boy.<br><br><br>This is the first book in the two book Omnibus <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_2_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Theft of Swords</a>. I picked this up from Audible and Tim Gerard Reynolds did a great job of the audio narration. His voice acting was superb and easy to listen to.<br><br>The book itself was lots of fun. I enjoyed the banter between the two main protagonists. They reminded me loosely of Locke and Jean in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/643750.The_Lies_of_Locke_Lamora__Gentleman_Bastard___1_" title="The Lies of Locke Lamora (Gentleman Bastard, #1) by Scott Lynch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lies of Locke Lamora</a> - being thieves and all and one guy being the muscle<br><br><b>
  <u>Hadrian</u>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385816452i/7236020.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(No, it doesn't look anything like Spartacus)<br><br>and one guy being the master thief<br><br><b>
  <u>Royce</u>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385815274i/7235744.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>It's a debut novel, and it feels like it - but Michael J Sullivan's writing improved noticeably over the course of the few hundred pages comprising his first book. Sure, the world building is kinda spoon fed to the reader and the characterization is a little light and the plot tends to telegraph what's coming up next - but the story just keeps rolling forward at an even pace, moving us from A to B to C without giving us any time to get bogged down or bored with the scenery. It worked. And this is just the first of six books (or three 2 book Omnibuses) in a completed series - so I'm looking forward to learning more about Royce and Hadrian given that Sullivan dropped in hints of the pair's past through the story. I see a lot of potential to really develop the characters and expand on the world building.<br><br>So If you are looking for a break from grimdark, or dark fantasy in general, and you are looking for something that will give the grey matter a bit of a break with some light and easy reading, then try this on for size. I enjoyed it.<br><br><br>3.5 stars<br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3949518188268011848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1289867683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289867683" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289867683?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5586102-the-crown-conspiracy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=dr-reading-challenge">dr-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289867683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4529316591972234712">After plowing through a few grimdark novels of significant size this year, I was thirsting for something less mentally exhausting and more fun to read. <br/><br/>Enter Riyria! And what a breath of fresh air this has been.<br/><br/>The Crown Conspiracy is probably the shortest in the series making it a really quick read. It is good introduction to the Riyria duo, Hadrian and Royce, who seemed to be more than what they appear to be on the surface and were complete opposites. Barely 3 chapters in and I was already hav</span>
  <span id="freeText4529316591972234712" style="display:none">After plowing through a few grimdark novels of significant size this year, I was thirsting for something less mentally exhausting and more fun to read. <br /><br />Enter Riyria! And what a breath of fresh air this has been.<br /><br />The Crown Conspiracy is probably the shortest in the series making it a really quick read. It is good introduction to the Riyria duo, Hadrian and Royce, who seemed to be more than what they appear to be on the surface and were complete opposites. Barely 3 chapters in and I was already having a mini crush on Hadrian, the classic warrior hero who is tall, handsome and has a cheerful demeanour - and he carries 3 swords!! I think that was the clincher for me (one does not carry 3 swords unless he really knows how to use them). Royce’s character was a bit harder to warm up to – the thief who probably grew up in harsh conditions and honed to be terribly effective in what he does (he does a dry sense of humour though). But together, the pair just seemed to <i>work</i> and their banter was funny and entertaining.<br /><br />The plot was simple (the blurb summarises it quite succinctly), the pacing decent with adequate action and elements of danger and mystery. The book just flew by very quickly for me. I have mentioned before that I’m not particular about prose in general, and I appreciate the simple manner of storytelling that was employed by the author. <br /><br />This is so far leaning more towards what I will refer to as classic fantasy although it's not exactly as traditional as, say, the Belgariad. It's lighthearted and fun, with just the right dose of action, magic and a main character that I can swoon over. What can I say, well-written fantasy tropes can be just plain fun sometimes!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4529316591972234712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6454110004657404354">I so enjoyed this book..and it's all due to what it lacks!<br/><br/>So much sword and sorcery fantasy these days feels like it has to be uber-descriptive. They remind me of the frozen turkeys that when you unthaw them just drain off water they have been 'plumped up' with. <br/><br/>So it was with great pleasure that I read this book: Despite an evil plot to overthrow the throne, sinister manipulations, secret prisons,a bratty prince and princess, an uber-magician, and a tenacious dwarf, the book seemed as refreshin</span>
  <span id="freeText6454110004657404354" style="display:none">I so enjoyed this book..and it's all due to what it lacks!<br /><br />So much sword and sorcery fantasy these days feels like it has to be uber-descriptive. They remind me of the frozen turkeys that when you unthaw them just drain off water they have been 'plumped up' with. <br /><br />So it was with great pleasure that I read this book: Despite an evil plot to overthrow the throne, sinister manipulations, secret prisons,a bratty prince and princess, an uber-magician, and a tenacious dwarf, the book seemed as refreshing as air!<br /><br /> the descriptions were there yet not overpowering. The author did not feel the need to add three adverbs and two adjectives to every sentence.The action scenes were to the point....no fillers! How refreshing this was!</span>

  <i>Unexpectedly, I liked this one very much.</i>
</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440164153i/15939503._SY540_.jpg" height="960" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Hadrian Blackwater and Royce Melborn</b>, infamous <b>Riyria</b> thieves, find themselves framed for the murder of the king. Whoever had the bright idea to pick those two to pin the crime on ... was a moron of epic proportions. Royce and Hadrian stand not for such nonsense.<br><br>Not a kind of epic fantasy I usually love. On the top of my epic fantasy list are authors like <i>Steven Erikson</i> and <i>Mark Lawrence</i>, with <i>meatier</i> writing ... and as for thieves and their masterful schemes, I recently read <i>The lies of Locke Lamora</i> ... so better schemes than those are hard to come to. <br>Still, it's highly entertaining.<br><br>This feels like fantasy <i>lite</i> (like a <i>buddy</i> movie, you know ... Rush Hour, Lethal Weapon, Bad Boys, in fantasy setting), yet I enjoyed it from beginning to end. So far, we only get a glimpse of the world where the story unfolds, and a glimpse of secrets that are for now.... far from being discovered.<br><br>Apart from the main duo (they are hilarious) I loved the most Myron, the young monk ( LOL his comparing horses and women), the Pickerings, and that evil dwarf (best villain of this book if you ask me).<br><br>In any case, I think I found another favorite series, <i>lite</i> or not.<br><br><b>
  <i> “So,” Royce said, “you want us to escape from this prison, kidnap the king, cross the countryside with him in tow while dodging soldiers who I assume might not accept our side of the story, and go to another secret prison so that he can visit an inmate?” </i>
</b></span>
