<span id="freeTextContainer35455854991499936">It has me <b>very</b> interested in continuing the story for sure. It is really a 3.75 stars, but at this stage I can't give it a 4. I am hoping, from reading all of my friends comments that the series develops well. I can see that happening. There has been some very nice character building (the narration on audio is excellent), but I really want to see a development of said characters now to push this story into the 4 star realm. Secondly, I want to see a bit more depth to the story, this did feel at </span>
  <span id="freeText35455854991499936" style="display:none">It has me <b>very</b> interested in continuing the story for sure. It is really a 3.75 stars, but at this stage I can't give it a 4. I am hoping, from reading all of my friends comments that the series develops well. I can see that happening. There has been some very nice character building (the narration on audio is excellent), but I really want to see a development of said characters now to push this story into the 4 star realm. Secondly, I want to see a bit more depth to the story, this did feel at times like a novella, but having already started the next book (1 chapter) I can see the thread is carrying on. There were parts to this book where I felt the story was rushed and large chunks of emotional story building were just not there and so at times I felt that i didn't have enough buy in to care. That sounds way harsher than I mean it to, but I am crap at trying to explain it any better. <br /><br />So my impression is, that the author has this huge idea and being the first part of the story is trying to get it all down and get into other parts and worrying that people will get bored with the details of like, raising an army and marching to a siege, so why not just make it happen next page, you know, like it happened in the ad break and then we can get back to the action bits. <br /><br />I am confident that this will change, bear in mind I read a lot of Erikson, Hamilton and Reynolds, not ones for skipping bits, too much info some might say, but that is the reading field I am coming from, so this was short on detail for me to give it the 4 stars.<br /><br />Looking forward to book 2. </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer178324471121022413">Looking for a fun book to read, which will take your mind off your daily problems? Look no further, as Michael J. Sullivan’s Riyria Revelations does just that. I am no fantasy aficionado and quite frankly haven’t really delved that deep into this genre. However, I can say without any hesitation that while this book may not be great as per fantasy nerd standards, it does make you enjoy every moment that you spend reading it. <br/><br/>This is a short book and only the first in the series, therefore it does</span>
  <span id="freeText178324471121022413" style="display:none">Looking for a fun book to read, which will take your mind off your daily problems? Look no further, as Michael J. Sullivan’s Riyria Revelations does just that. I am no fantasy aficionado and quite frankly haven’t really delved that deep into this genre. However, I can say without any hesitation that while this book may not be great as per fantasy nerd standards, it does make you enjoy every moment that you spend reading it. <br /><br />This is a short book and only the first in the series, therefore it doesn’t do well to go into it with a lot of expectations. In fact, I went into it with zero expectations and was pleasantly surprised and totally entertained, so much so that I had to pick up book 2 immediately. Being a small book, it does not really go deep into either character development or world building, which I agree could be a problem for most fantasy buffs. However, I choose to look at this book as an interesting appetizer instead of a full course meal; something that whets your appetite without really making you full. Given that there are 6 books in this series and another 2 or more that explain the background, I was quite satisfied with what this had to offer. <br /><br />Looking at the characters now, especially the protagonists, Hadrian and Royce – I just loved them. Their interactions were funny and entertaining, as were their roles. They are two thieves who get a high out of flummoxing people and taking up undoable tasks and getting them done in the most creative ways possible. Their friendship was simply superb and their feelings for each other came out really well, although I would have loved a little more of that. Of all the other characters that were in support, I loved Myron the best. I mean how could I not like a nerdy monk who could recite pages after pages from all the books that he had read? Also, there was this fact that he was totally isolated from everything as he grew up in the monastery, so it was refreshing to see the world from his view, a view that hasn’t been tarnished by any kind of cynicism or negativity. <br /><br />The basic plot in this book is extremely simple and was quite predictable, which was another problem but somehow I enjoyed it despite its simplicity and predictability. I mean I had the suspect clearly identified when the murder happened but there was this story arc that was going parallel to the main story in this book, which had links to the future books in the series, which made me like the book a little better, if only for its intrigue value. <br /><br />This was one ‘paisa vasool’ kind of book, wherein you get your money’s worth in terms of entertainment, provided of course you are not looking for great depth and darker realms and the like. If you go in, as I did, looking for pure entertainment, you won’t be disappointed. However, if you are looking for dark fantasy or epic fantasy where you will get great plots and characters and different twists and the like, you are bound to be disappointed and this book is not for you.<br /><br />Am definitely going to read the next one to see which way this particular river flows. While I do that, check this out with an open mind and you might just be entertained like I was. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="178324471121022413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_36601965" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36601965" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1009204-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1228465282p2/1009204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36601965?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/1009204-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1009204-cindy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1009204-cindy?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36601965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8821536332025275920">Thrilling, Captivating, Amazing are some of the first words that came to mind when I finished this book last night. I stayed up late into the night to finish this book, so that is a sign that I loved it. One of the better sword and sorcery books that I have come across in a while. <br/><br/>This book was a take back to the fantasy books that have quests, magic, and great characters and plots. At first I wasn't sure if I was really going to bond with any of the characters, but to my delight I found myself </span>
  <span id="freeText8821536332025275920" style="display:none">Thrilling, Captivating, Amazing are some of the first words that came to mind when I finished this book last night. I stayed up late into the night to finish this book, so that is a sign that I loved it. One of the better sword and sorcery books that I have come across in a while. <br /><br />This book was a take back to the fantasy books that have quests, magic, and great characters and plots. At first I wasn't sure if I was really going to bond with any of the characters, but to my delight I found myself loving Royce and Hadrian. There was a touch of humor that didn't come across as forced, a lot of books try to force the reader to laugh and I found myself chuckling at a couple of the jokes between the two. <br /><br />There is a tiny bit of magic and of course a wizard, which isn't too complicated. I think this is great for anyone that is a fantasy lover or for teens who are starting out in the fantasy section of their library. I get frustrated when the magic in books is so complicated I feel I have to take notes, this wasn't the case at all. <br /><br />The plot was swift but not swift enough that I found myself lost or parts over looked.Sullivan had a real skill in keeping the plot going and knowing just when to throw that curve ball in the plot or at what time it was perfect to reveal a certain crucial part of the plot to the readers! I was never left waiting too long to find out when something was going to happen but I was still sitting on the edge of my seat waiting for the next part of the book.<br /><br />I loved that it was a stand alone novel of a series. The plot was wrapped up but there were parts of the book that were left open for the next book and the series beyond. A lot of series force the reader to wait till the next book to learn more, Sullivan can keep a reader and continue a series without leaving major cliff hanger and helps with the frustration of having to wait years for a book! <br /><br />It's hard to find something to complain about in this book. Like any first time writers I look forward to seeing Sullivan grow as an author and I hope that in future books we get to know some more characters. <br /><br />I highly recommend reading this book, whether your a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84136.Fantasy_Lover__Dark_Hunter___1_" title="Fantasy Lover (Dark-Hunter, #1) by Sherrilyn Kenyon" rel="nofollow noopener">fantasy lover</a> or just looking to start out in it. I personally have recommended it to my family and anyone that will listen to read. It was good to see a lovely written fantasy/adventure novel. This book has found a place on my reading shelves next to my Terry Brooks books and of course Harry Potter. I really can't wait till the next book in the series! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8821536332025275920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		    <b>
          <a title="What&#39;s the Name of That Book???" class="actionLink" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/19682416-solved-fantasy-a-young-male-has-to-get-a-sword-from-a-tower-by-swimming">What&#39;s the Name o...:</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('P2ODft5y7BcnLQi8l3iz1hzmTko8W8iUTzjpYoXuB6CSWOE5FGxZElwWYk5tzpAh+PTmzsNFH/hLI88tBWaz5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dGt9rUVFq//bFZ1AN7xUcABtrBxa6IeiN+QbgphxRznZUB/qj1se+qAu97LNCneH5H8EmKX2UM4z/z3NGPnzfw==')})
  }
